### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between the state and the nation, two fundamental concepts in the study of territoriality. The state, as a political entity, and the nation, as a cultural and social construct, have been intertwined throughout history, shaping and reshaping each other in a dynamic and ever-changing landscape.

The state, with its boundaries and sovereignty, is often seen as the primary source of territoriality. It is the state that defines and controls the physical space within its boundaries, and it is the state that exercises power over its inhabitants. However, the nation, with its shared cultural and social identity, can also be a powerful force in shaping territoriality. The idea of a nation, with its shared history, language, and customs, can create a sense of belonging and identity that transcends the boundaries of the state.

In this chapter, we will explore the historical and contemporary dynamics of the state and the nation, and how they interact to create and shape territoriality. We will also examine the role of power in this relationship, and how it is used to define and control territoriality.

As we navigate through this complex and multifaceted topic, we will also touch upon the concept of spatial reification, a key concept in understanding territoriality. Spatial reification, the process of transforming abstract concepts into tangible spaces, is a crucial aspect of territoriality. It is through this process that the state and the nation are able to assert their power and control over physical space.

Join us as we journey through the intricate world of the state and the nation, and explore the fascinating dynamics of territoriality.




### Subsection: 17.1 Power & Space:

#### 17.1a Power Dynamics

The dynamics of power in the context of state and nation are complex and multifaceted. Power, in this context, can be understood as the ability of a state or a nation to influence events and decisions. It is a crucial factor in shaping territoriality, as it is through the exercise of power that states and nations are able to assert their control over physical space.

The concept of power is deeply intertwined with the concept of sovereignty. Sovereignty, in the context of the state, refers to the supreme authority of a state over itself. It is the state's power to govern itself without any interference from external powers. The concept of sovereignty is often used to justify the state's control over its territory. The state's power to define and control its territory is seen as a manifestation of its sovereignty.

However, the concept of sovereignty is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute sovereignty, where a state's power is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of sovereignty is now understood in terms of relative sovereignty, where a state's power is constrained by international law and norms. This relative sovereignty is often seen in the context of the state's power over its territory. While the state has the power to govern its territory, this power is not absolute. It is constrained by international law and norms, such as the prohibition of genocide, torture, and other human rights violations.

The concept of sovereignty is also closely tied to the concept of territoriality. Territoriality, in the context of the state, refers to the state's power to define and control its territory. This power is often seen as a manifestation of the state's sovereignty. However, the concept of territoriality is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of territoriality is now understood in terms of relative territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is constrained by international law and norms.

In the context of the nation, power dynamics are often shaped by the idea of national identity. National identity, in this context, refers to the shared cultural and social identity of a nation. This shared identity can be a powerful force in shaping territoriality, as it can create a sense of belonging and identity that transcends the boundaries of the state. However, the concept of national identity is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute national identity, where a nation's power is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of national identity is now understood in terms of relative national identity, where a nation's power is constrained by international law and norms.

In conclusion, the dynamics of power in the context of state and nation are complex and multifaceted. Power, in this context, is often understood in terms of sovereignty and territoriality. However, these concepts are not without their complexities, and they are often shaped by international law and norms.

#### 17.1b Power & Space

The relationship between power and space is a crucial aspect of understanding territoriality. Power, in this context, is not just about the ability to influence events and decisions, but also about the ability to shape and control physical space. This is particularly evident in the context of the state and nation, where power dynamics often play out in the spatial realm.

The state, as a political entity, exercises power over its territory through various means. This includes the power to define and control the physical space within its boundaries. The state's power over its territory is often seen as a manifestation of its sovereignty. However, this power is not absolute. It is constrained by international law and norms, such as the prohibition of genocide, torture, and other human rights violations.

The concept of sovereignty is closely tied to the concept of territoriality. Territoriality, in the context of the state, refers to the state's power to define and control its territory. This power is often seen as a manifestation of the state's sovereignty. However, the concept of territoriality is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of territoriality is now understood in terms of relative territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is constrained by international law and norms.

In the context of the nation, power dynamics are often shaped by the idea of national identity. National identity, in this context, refers to the shared cultural and social identity of a nation. This shared identity can be a powerful force in shaping territoriality, as it can create a sense of belonging and identity that transcends the boundaries of the state. However, the concept of national identity is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute national identity, where a nation's power is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of national identity is now understood in terms of relative national identity, where a nation's power is constrained by international law and norms.

The relationship between power and space is also evident in the context of the International Space Station (ISS). The ISS, as a spatial entity, is governed by a complex set of power dynamics. These dynamics are shaped by the power of various states and nations to influence the station's operations and decisions. The ISS is a prime example of how power and space intersect in the context of territoriality.

In conclusion, the relationship between power and space is a crucial aspect of understanding territoriality. Power, in this context, is not just about the ability to influence events and decisions, but also about the ability to shape and control physical space. This is particularly evident in the context of the state and nation, where power dynamics often play out in the spatial realm.

#### 17.1c Case Studies

To further illustrate the complex relationship between power and space, let's delve into some case studies. These case studies will provide concrete examples of how power dynamics play out in the spatial realm, particularly in the context of the state and nation.

##### Case Study 1: The International Space Station (ISS)

The International Space Station (ISS) is a prime example of how power and space intersect in the context of territoriality. The ISS is a multinational collaborative project between NASA (United States), Roscosmos (Russia), ESA (Europe), JAXA (Japan), and CSA (Canada). Each of these nations has a significant stake in the ISS, and their power dynamics play out in the spatial realm of the station.

For instance, the power and thermal control systems of the ISS are a testament to the complex power dynamics at play. The Russian segment of the station, like most spacecraft, uses 28 V low voltage DC from two rotating solar arrays mounted on "Zvezda". The USOS, on the other hand, uses 130–180 V DC from the USOS PV array. This difference in power systems is a reflection of the different technological capabilities and power dynamics of the US and Russia in the context of space exploration.

The USOS solar arrays are arranged as four wing pairs, for a total production of 75 to 90 kilowatts. These arrays normally track the Sun to maximize power generation. Each array is about 10 m long and 4 m wide. The station's large solar panels generate a high potential voltage difference between the station and the ionosphere, which is a significant factor in the station's power dynamics.

##### Case Study 2: The State of Israel

The State of Israel provides another interesting case study of power and space. Israel's power dynamics are shaped by its unique geographical location, its history of conflict, and its political and social dynamics. The state's power over its territory is often seen as a manifestation of its sovereignty. However, this power is not absolute. It is constrained by international law and norms, such as the prohibition of genocide, torture, and other human rights violations.

The concept of sovereignty is closely tied to the concept of territoriality in Israel. Territoriality, in the context of Israel, refers to the state's power to define and control its territory. This power is often seen as a manifestation of the state's sovereignty. However, the concept of territoriality is not without its complexities. The idea of absolute territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is unlimited and unconstrained, has been largely discredited in modern international law. The concept of territoriality is now understood in terms of relative territoriality, where a state's power over its territory is constrained by international law and norms.

In conclusion, these case studies illustrate the complex relationship between power and space. They show how power dynamics play out in the spatial realm, particularly in the context of the state and nation. They also highlight the importance of understanding these dynamics in the study of territoriality.




### Subsection: 17.2 Initial Mapping and Research Topic Presentations:

#### 17.2a Mapping Techniques

Mapping techniques are essential tools in the study of state and nation. They allow us to visualize and analyze the spatial aspects of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty. In this section, we will explore some of the most commonly used mapping techniques in the study of state and nation.

##### Power Mapping

Power mapping is a technique used to visualize the distribution of power within a given territory. It involves identifying and mapping the sources of power, such as political parties, economic institutions, and social groups, and their relative influence. This technique can be particularly useful in understanding the dynamics of power within a state or nation, and how these dynamics shape territoriality and sovereignty.

##### Geographic Information Systems (GIS)

Geographic Information Systems (GIS) are powerful tools for analyzing and visualizing spatial data. They allow us to map and analyze complex spatial data, such as land use, population density, and migration patterns. GIS can be particularly useful in the study of state and nation, as it allows us to visualize and analyze the spatial aspects of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty.

##### Web Mapping

Web mapping is a technique that involves creating and sharing maps on the internet. Web mapping tools, such as Google Maps and ArcGIS Online, allow us to create and share maps easily and quickly. Web mapping can be particularly useful in the study of state and nation, as it allows us to share maps and data with a wide audience, and facilitates collaboration among researchers.

##### Animated and Real-time Mapping

Animated and real-time mapping techniques allow us to visualize changes in a territory over time. Animated maps show changes in the map over time by animating one of the graphical or temporal variables. Real-time maps, on the other hand, show the current situation of a phenomenon in close to real-time. These techniques can be particularly useful in the study of state and nation, as they allow us to track changes in power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty over time.

In the next section, we will explore how these mapping techniques can be used in research topic presentations.

#### 17.2b Research Topic Presentations

Research topic presentations are an integral part of the learning process in the study of state and nation. They provide an opportunity for students to delve deeper into specific aspects of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty, and to share their findings with their peers. In this section, we will discuss the importance of research topic presentations, and provide some tips for preparing and delivering effective presentations.

##### Importance of Research Topic Presentations

Research topic presentations are a valuable learning tool. They allow students to explore a topic of interest in depth, and to develop their research and presentation skills. They also provide an opportunity for students to learn from each other, as they share their findings and insights. 

In the context of state and nation, research topic presentations can help students to understand the complexities of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty. They can also help students to develop a critical understanding of these concepts, and to see them in a broader context.

##### Preparing for Research Topic Presentations

Preparing for a research topic presentation involves several steps. First, students need to choose a topic that interests them, and that is relevant to the course. This can be done in consultation with the course instructor.

Next, students need to conduct research on their chosen topic. This can involve reading academic articles, books, and other sources, and collecting and analyzing data. It's important for students to use reliable sources, and to properly cite all sources used in their presentation.

Once the research is complete, students need to organize their findings and develop a clear and coherent presentation. This can involve creating a map or other visual aids, and developing a script or outline for the presentation.

##### Delivering Research Topic Presentations

Delivering a research topic presentation can be a nerve-wracking experience, but with preparation and practice, it can be a rewarding one. Here are some tips for delivering an effective presentation:

- Practice your presentation beforehand, ideally in front of a small audience. This can help you to become more familiar with your material, and to identify and address any potential issues.

- Start your presentation with a clear introduction, including an overview of your topic, your research question, and your key findings.

- Use visual aids, such as maps or charts, to help illustrate your points.

- Speak clearly and confidently, and make eye contact with your audience.

- Allow time for questions and discussion at the end of your presentation. This can be a valuable learning opportunity, as it allows you to engage with your audience and to learn from their insights.

In conclusion, research topic presentations are a valuable learning tool in the study of state and nation. They provide an opportunity for students to delve deeper into specific aspects of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty, and to share their findings with their peers. With proper preparation and practice, students can deliver effective and engaging presentations.

#### 17.2c Presentation Feedback

After the research topic presentations, it is crucial to provide feedback to the presenters. This feedback can be in the form of a written report or an oral discussion. The feedback should be constructive and aimed at helping the presenter improve their presentation skills and research.

##### Importance of Presentation Feedback

Presentation feedback is an essential part of the learning process. It allows students to understand their strengths and weaknesses, and to identify areas for improvement. In the context of state and nation, presentation feedback can help students to develop a deeper understanding of the complexities of power dynamics, territoriality, and sovereignty.

Moreover, presentation feedback can also help to create a learning community. By providing feedback to their peers, students can learn from each other's research and presentation skills. This can foster a sense of collaboration and mutual learning.

##### Guidelines for Providing Presentation Feedback

When providing presentation feedback, it is important to follow some guidelines. These guidelines can help to ensure that the feedback is constructive and helpful.

1. Be specific: Instead of making general statements, focus on specific aspects of the presentation. This can include the structure of the presentation, the clarity of the arguments, the use of visual aids, and the delivery of the presentation.

2. Be balanced: While it is important to point out areas for improvement, also highlight the strengths of the presentation. This can help to motivate the presenter and to build their confidence.

3. Be actionable: The feedback should include specific suggestions for improvement. This can include recommendations for further research, suggestions for improving the structure or delivery of the presentation, or advice on how to handle questions from the audience.

4. Be respectful: Remember that the presenter has put a lot of effort into their presentation. Be respectful in your feedback, and avoid personal attacks.

5. Be timely: Provide the feedback in a timely manner. This can help to ensure that the presenter can still use the feedback for their final presentation.

By following these guidelines, you can provide effective and helpful presentation feedback. This can contribute to a positive learning experience for both the presenter and the feedback provider.

## Chapter: Chapter 18: Globalization

### Introduction

In the realm of geography, the concept of globalization has been a subject of intense study and debate. This chapter, "Globalization," aims to delve into the intricate dynamics of globalization, its implications, and its spatial reification of power. 

Globalization, in the context of geography, refers to the process of interaction and integration among people, companies, and governments worldwide. It is a phenomenon that has been accelerated by advancements in technology, transportation, and communication, leading to a more interconnected and interdependent global economy. 

The concept of globalization is not without its critics. Some argue that it has led to the homogenization of cultures, the exploitation of resources, and the widening of the gap between the rich and the poor. Others contend that it has facilitated the flow of goods, services, and ideas, leading to economic growth and development. 

This chapter will explore these perspectives, examining the spatial aspects of globalization and its impact on power dynamics. We will delve into the ways in which globalization has reconfigured power relations, creating new centers of power and challenging traditional power structures. 

We will also explore the role of space in globalization, examining how space is both a product and a producer of globalization. We will look at how globalization has transformed the way we perceive and interact with space, and how it has led to the creation of new spatial categories and identities. 

In this chapter, we will also discuss the implications of globalization for geography, exploring how it has changed the way we study and understand the world. We will examine the challenges and opportunities that globalization presents for geography, and how it has forced us to rethink our theories and methods. 

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of globalization, its spatial aspects, and its implications for power dynamics. It is our hope that this chapter will not only deepen your understanding of globalization but also stimulate your thinking about the complex and multifaceted nature of this phenomenon.




### Subsection: 17.3 Reification - Marx, Lukács, and Beyond:

#### 17.3a Marx and Lukács on Reification

The concept of reification, as we have seen, is a critical concept in Marxist thought. It is a process by which human creations, such as social relations, are misconceived as natural or divine entities. This process, according to Marx and Lukács, is a result of the commodity form prevalent in capitalist society.

Marx, in his "The Fetishism of the Commodity and its Secret", introduces the concept of reification by discussing the fetishism of commodities. He argues that in a capitalist society, commodities are not just objects of utility or exchange, but also objects of veneration. This veneration, Marx suggests, is a form of reification, as it transforms commodities into objects of worship, thereby obscuring the social relations that underpin their existence.

Lukács, in his "History and Class Consciousness", further develops this concept. He argues that reification is a problem of capitalist society that is related to the prevalence of the commodity form. According to Lukács, reification affects the consciousness of the proletariat, leading them to misconceive their social relations as natural or divine entities. This, Lukács argues, is a form of false consciousness that prevents the proletariat from understanding their true social position and their potential for revolutionary change.

Lukács's account of reification was influential for the philosophers of the Frankfurt School, such as Horkheimer and Adorno, who argued that reification is a result of the "dialectic of enlightenment". They argued that the Enlightenment's emphasis on rationality and objectivity had led to the reification of human relations, thereby undermining the potential for emancipatory social change.

More recently, Axel Honneth, a Frankfurt School philosopher, has reformulated this "Western Marxist" concept in terms of intersubjective relations of recognition and power. Honneth contends that all forms of reification are due to pathologies of intersubjectively based struggles for recognition. This reformulation highlights the importance of intersubjective relations in the process of reification, thereby expanding our understanding of this critical Marxist concept.

In the next section, we will explore the implications of reification for the study of state and nation, and how this concept can help us understand the spatial reification of power in these entities.

#### 17.3b Critiques of Reification

The concept of reification, while influential, has been subject to various critiques. These critiques have been directed at both the Marxist and Frankfurt School interpretations of reification.

One of the main critiques of reification is its alleged reductionism. Critics argue that by reducing social relations to objects, reification obscures the complex and dynamic nature of social life. This reductionism, they argue, is a result of the Marxist and Frankfurt School interpretations of reification, which focus on the commodity form and intersubjective relations, respectively.

Another critique of reification is its alleged essentialism. Critics argue that by treating social relations as objects, reification essentializes these relations, thereby obscuring their historical and contextual specificity. This essentialism, they argue, is a result of the Marxist and Frankfurt School interpretations of reification, which focus on the commodity form and intersubjective relations, respectively.

A third critique of reification is its alleged determinism. Critics argue that by treating social relations as objects, reification determinizes these relations, thereby obscuring the potential for human agency and social change. This determinism, they argue, is a result of the Marxist and Frankfurt School interpretations of reification, which focus on the commodity form and intersubjective relations, respectively.

Despite these critiques, reification remains a critical concept in Marxist thought. It provides a powerful tool for analyzing the ways in which human creations are misconceived as natural or divine entities in capitalist society. Furthermore, the critiques of reification have led to important developments in Marxist thought, such as the concept of intersubjective recognition proposed by Honneth.

In the next section, we will explore the implications of these critiques for the study of state and nation, and how they can be used to develop a more nuanced understanding of the spatial reification of power.

#### 17.3c Beyond Reification: Post-Marxist Perspectives

The concept of reification, as we have seen, has been a central concept in Marxist thought. However, post-Marxist perspectives have sought to move beyond reification, proposing alternative ways of understanding the relationship between social relations and objects.

One such perspective is the post-Marxist theory of "object-oriented ontology" (OOO). OOO proposes a radical departure from the Marxist tradition, arguing that objects, not social relations, are the primary ontological category. This perspective rejects the Marxist notion of reification, arguing instead that objects have their own ontological status, independent of human consciousness or social relations.

OOO also rejects the Marxist critique of reification, arguing that it is not reductionist or essentialist. Instead, OOO argues that objects are complex and dynamic, and that their essence is not reducible to their properties or relations. Furthermore, OOO argues that objects are not deterministic, as they are capable of exercising agency and influencing social relations.

Another post-Marxist perspective is the post-structuralist theory of "actor-network theory" (ANT). ANT proposes a middle ground between the Marxist and OOO perspectives, arguing that both objects and social relations are important ontological categories. ANT rejects the Marxist notion of reification, arguing instead that objects and social relations are co-constitutive, each influencing and being influenced by the other.

ANT also rejects the Marxist critique of reification, arguing that it is not reductionist or essentialist. Instead, ANT argues that objects and social relations are complex and dynamic, and that their essence is not reducible to their properties or relations. Furthermore, ANT argues that objects and social relations are not deterministic, as they are capable of exercising agency and influencing each other.

In conclusion, while the concept of reification has been a central concept in Marxist thought, post-Marxist perspectives have sought to move beyond reification, proposing alternative ways of understanding the relationship between social relations and objects. These post-Marxist perspectives offer valuable insights into the complex and dynamic nature of social life, and their exploration is an important task for future research.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between state and nation, and how they are spatial reifications of power. We have seen how the state, as a political entity, exercises power over a defined territory, while the nation, as a cultural entity, claims a shared identity and history within that territory. This relationship is not static, but dynamic, shaped by a multitude of factors including historical context, economic conditions, and social dynamics.

We have also examined how these two entities are not always aligned, with the state often seeking to impose its power over the nation, leading to conflicts and tensions. Conversely, the nation can also challenge the state's authority, leading to struggles for self-determination and independence. These dynamics are further complicated by the presence of multiple states and nations within a territory, leading to complex power struggles and negotiations.

In conclusion, the state and nation are not just abstract concepts, but spatial reifications of power, shaped by a multitude of factors and dynamics. Understanding these dynamics is crucial for understanding power dynamics in any society.

## Chapter: Chapter 18: Globalization

### Introduction

In this chapter, we delve into the complex and multifaceted concept of globalization. Globalization, a term that has become ubiquitous in our modern world, is a phenomenon that has been shaping the political, economic, and cultural landscapes of our planet for centuries. It is a process that has been accelerated by advancements in technology, transportation, and communication, leading to the interconnectedness of nations and cultures in ways that were unimaginable a few decades ago.

Globalization is not just about the physical interconnectedness of nations. It is also about the reification of power, the spatial manifestation of power dynamics on a global scale. It is about how power is exercised, contested, and negotiated in a world where boundaries are increasingly blurred and where the local is often influenced by, and intertwined with, the global.

In this chapter, we will explore the various dimensions of globalization, including its economic, political, and cultural aspects. We will also delve into the power dynamics that underpin globalization, examining how power is reified in space and how it shapes the global landscape. We will look at how globalization has transformed the world, creating new opportunities and challenges, and how it continues to shape our lives in profound ways.

As we navigate through this chapter, we will also grapple with the complexities and contradictions of globalization. We will examine the ways in which globalization has been both a force for progress and a source of inequality, conflict, and environmental degradation. We will also explore the ways in which globalization has been both a product and a driver of spatial reification, shaping the power dynamics of our world in profound ways.

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of globalization, not just as a process of economic integration, but as a spatial reification of power. It aims to shed light on the complex and multifaceted nature of globalization, and to equip readers with the tools to critically engage with this phenomenon.

In conclusion, the state and the nation are two interconnected entities that shape and are shaped by the concept of territory. Their relationship is complex and multifaceted, and understanding it is crucial for comprehending the dynamics of power and ownership in the modern world.

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the theories surrounding world urbanization. Urbanization is a complex phenomenon that has been shaping the world for centuries. It is the process by which a society becomes more urban, with a greater proportion of people living in cities. This shift has significant implications for social, economic, and political structures, making it a crucial topic to explore in the study of territorial power.

We will begin by examining the historical context of urbanization, tracing its roots back to ancient civilizations. We will then explore the theories that explain the causes and consequences of urbanization, including the Marxian theory of urbanization, the Weberian theory of urbanization, and the Rostovian theory of urbanization. These theories provide different perspectives on the role of urbanization in society, offering insights into the spatial reification of power.

Furthermore, we will discuss the current state of urbanization in the world, examining the trends and patterns that have emerged in recent years. This will include a discussion on the urbanization of the global south, the rise of megacities, and the challenges and opportunities that come with these developments.

Finally, we will explore the future of urbanization, considering the potential implications of continued urbanization for territorial power and the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead. This will include a discussion on the potential for sustainable urban development and the role of urbanization in addressing global challenges such as climate change and inequality.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the theories surrounding world urbanization and its implications for territorial power. This knowledge will provide a solid foundation for further exploration into the complex and ever-evolving world of urbanization.




### Subsection: 18.1 World Urbanization - Architecture Reactions:

Urbanization has had a profound impact on the built environment, leading to the development of unique architectural styles that reflect the cultural, social, and economic influences of the urban landscape. In this section, we will explore the various architectural reactions to urbanization, with a focus on the modernist movement.

#### 18.1a Modernist Architecture

Modernist architecture emerged in the early 20th century as a response to the rapid urbanization and industrialization of the time. It was characterized by a break from traditional architectural styles and a focus on functionality, simplicity, and the use of new materials and technologies. Modernist architects sought to create buildings that were in harmony with the urban environment, reflecting the changing social and cultural values of the time.

One of the key principles of modernist architecture was the concept of "form follows function," which emphasized the importance of a building's functionality over its aesthetic. This was a departure from the ornate and decorative styles of the past, and it reflected the changing values of a society that was increasingly focused on efficiency and progress.

Modernist architecture also embraced the use of new materials and technologies, such as steel, glass, and concrete. These materials allowed for the creation of large, open spaces and the use of natural light, which were seen as essential for the well-being of urban dwellers. The use of these materials also reflected the industrial and technological influences of the urban landscape.

In addition to its functional and aesthetic aspects, modernist architecture also had a significant impact on the urban fabric. The use of new materials and technologies allowed for the creation of tall, multi-story buildings, which were essential for accommodating the growing urban population. This led to the development of skyscrapers, which became a defining feature of modern cities.

Modernist architecture also played a crucial role in shaping the urban landscape through its influence on urban planning. Modernist architects often worked closely with urban planners to create integrated designs that considered the overall layout and organization of a city. This led to the development of new urban forms, such as the grid-like layout of American cities, which were seen as more efficient and modern.

However, modernist architecture also faced criticism for its perceived lack of aesthetic appeal and its impact on the traditional urban fabric. Some argued that the use of new materials and technologies led to a homogenization of the urban landscape, with buildings looking similar regardless of their location. This led to the emergence of postmodernist architecture, which sought to address these concerns by incorporating elements of traditional architectural styles while still embracing modernist principles.

In conclusion, modernist architecture played a crucial role in shaping the urban landscape of the 20th century. Its focus on functionality, simplicity, and the use of new materials and technologies reflected the changing social and cultural values of the time. However, it also faced criticism, leading to the emergence of postmodernist architecture and a continued evolution of architectural styles in response to urbanization.





### Subsection: 18.2 Boundlessness, or Infinite Extension:

The concept of boundlessness, or infinite extension, is a fundamental aspect of urbanization. As cities continue to expand and evolve, they often seem to have no boundaries, with new developments and urban sprawl extending in all directions. This phenomenon can be seen in both physical and virtual urban spaces, as cities continue to expand and incorporate new technologies and digital spaces.

#### 18.2a Infinite Urbanization

The idea of infinite urbanization is closely tied to the concept of the Absolute Infinite, as proposed by mathematician Georg Cantor. Just as the Absolute Infinite is a number that is bigger than any other conceivable or inconceivable quantity, the urban landscape can also be seen as infinite in its extension and growth.

Cantor's idea of the Absolute Infinite was linked to the concept of God, and he believed that it had various mathematical properties. One of these properties, known as the reflection principle, states that every property of the Absolute Infinite is also held by some smaller object. This principle can also be applied to the urban landscape, as every aspect of the city can be found in smaller, more manageable forms.

However, the idea of infinite urbanization can also lead to paradoxes, similar to Cantor's idea of the Absolute Infinite. For example, the idea that the collection of all urban spaces cannot logically exist seems paradoxical to many. This is related to Cesare Burali-Forti's "paradox" which states that there can be no greatest urban space. All of these problems can be traced back to the idea that, for every property that can be logically defined, there exists a set of all objects that have that property. However, as in Cantor's argument, this idea leads to difficulties.

To address these paradoxes, some urban planners and architects have proposed solutions that limit the growth of urban spaces. For example, the concept of "smart cities" aims to create more sustainable and efficient urban spaces by using technology to manage and optimize resources. This approach can help to mitigate the negative effects of infinite urbanization, while still allowing for the growth and development of cities.

In conclusion, the concept of boundlessness, or infinite extension, is a crucial aspect of urbanization. It reflects the ever-expanding nature of cities and the challenges and opportunities that come with this growth. As we continue to urbanize, it is important to consider the implications of infinite urbanization and work towards creating more sustainable and livable cities for all.





### Subsection: 18.3 The Border:

The border is a crucial aspect of urbanization, as it serves as the boundary between two different urban spaces. It is a line that separates one city from another, or one neighborhood from another. The border can be physical, such as a wall or fence, or it can be conceptual, such as a line on a map. In this section, we will explore the concept of the border and its role in urbanization.

#### 18.3a Border Theory

The theory of the border is a fundamental concept in urbanization. It is based on the idea that the border is a line of separation between two different urban spaces. This line can be physical, such as a wall or fence, or it can be conceptual, such as a line on a map. The border serves as a boundary between two different urban spaces, and it plays a crucial role in shaping the identity and character of each space.

The theory of the border is closely tied to the concept of territoriality, as discussed in the previous section. Just as territoriality refers to the spatial reification of power, the border can be seen as a physical manifestation of this power. The border is a line that is drawn and enforced by those in power, and it serves as a symbol of their control over the urban space.

The border also plays a crucial role in shaping the social and cultural dynamics of urban spaces. As mentioned in the previous section, the border can be a site of conflict and tension, as different groups vie for control over the space. This can lead to the formation of distinct identities and cultures within each urban space, as each group seeks to assert its dominance and establish its own boundaries.

Furthermore, the border can also be a site of exchange and interaction between different urban spaces. As cities continue to expand and merge, the border can become a place of overlap and intermingling, where people and ideas from different urban spaces come together. This can lead to the formation of new urban spaces, with their own unique characteristics and identities.

In conclusion, the border is a crucial aspect of urbanization, serving as a line of separation and a symbol of power and control. Its role in shaping the identity and character of urban spaces, as well as its potential for exchange and interaction, makes it a fundamental concept in understanding the complexities of urbanization.

We have delved into the complex and multifaceted nature of urbanization, examining its causes, effects, and implications for society. We have also examined the role of power in urbanization, and how it is spatial reification. Power, in this context, is not just about who holds it, but also about how it is exercised and experienced. We have seen how power shapes the urban landscape, influencing everything from the physical layout of cities to the social and economic dynamics within them.

As we move forward, it is important to continue exploring and refining these theories, and to apply them to the ever-changing landscape of urbanization. By doing so, we can gain a more nuanced understanding of urbanization, and work towards creating more livable, equitable, and sustainable cities for all.

## Chapter: - Chapter 19: The Envelope:




### Section: 19.1 Territory, Not Land:

### Subsection: 19.1c Case Studies of Territory

In this section, we will explore some case studies that illustrate the concept of territory and its role in shaping power dynamics. These case studies will provide a deeper understanding of the complexities and nuances of territory and its impact on various aspects of society.

#### Case Study 1: The United States and its Territories

The United States is a prime example of a country with a complex territory. The country has a long history of territorial expansion, with its boundaries constantly changing over time. The U.S. has acquired territories through various means, including purchase, conquest, and annexation. These territories have played a significant role in shaping the country's power dynamics.

For instance, the U.S. acquired the Louisiana Territory in 1803, which doubled the country's size and provided access to valuable natural resources. This territory also played a crucial role in the country's westward expansion and the development of its economy. The U.S. also acquired the Hawaiian Islands in 1898, which served as a strategic military base and a source of valuable resources.

The U.S. has also had a complex relationship with its territories in the Caribbean and Pacific Islands. These territories have been used for various purposes, including military bases, labor camps, and tourist destinations. The U.S. has also faced criticism for its treatment of these territories, with some arguing that they are exploited for the benefit of the U.S. mainland.

#### Case Study 2: The European Union and its Member States

The European Union (EU) is another example of a complex territory. The EU is a political and economic union of 27 member states, with a combined population of over 446 million people. The EU has a unique territory, with its boundaries constantly evolving as new member states join and others leave.

The EU has a complex system of governance, with power being shared between the EU institutions and the member states. The EU has its own legal system, currency, and border controls. The EU also has a common external border, with member states sharing responsibility for protecting the EU's borders.

The EU's territory is also home to a diverse range of cultures, languages, and traditions. This diversity has led to the development of a unique European identity, with the EU promoting values such as democracy, human rights, and the rule of law.

#### Case Study 3: The Kingdom of Saudi Arabia

The Kingdom of Saudi Arabia (KSA) is a country with a vast territory, covering an area of over 2.15 million square kilometers. The KSA is home to the world's largest oil reserves, making it one of the most powerful and influential countries in the world.

The KSA's territory is largely desert, with a small portion of arable land. This has led to a heavy reliance on oil for the country's economy, with the government using its oil wealth to fund various development projects. The KSA's territory also includes the holy cities of Mecca and Medina, which are of great importance to Muslims around the world.

The KSA's territory is also home to a diverse range of ethnic groups, with the majority being Saudi Arabians. The country has a strict interpretation of Islam, with the government controlling many aspects of daily life. The KSA's territory is also home to a large number of foreign workers, who make up a significant portion of the country's population.

In conclusion, these case studies illustrate the complexities and nuances of territory and its role in shaping power dynamics. Each of these territories has its own unique characteristics and challenges, highlighting the importance of understanding territory in the study of power dynamics. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of territory and its role in shaping power dynamics. We have seen how territory is not just a physical space, but also a social and political construct that is constantly being redefined and contested. We have also examined the various ways in which territory is used to assert and maintain power, from colonialism to modern-day land grabs.

Through our exploration of the envelope, we have seen how territory is not a fixed entity, but rather a fluid and dynamic concept. The envelope is a powerful tool that allows us to understand the complexities of territory and its impact on power dynamics. By examining the envelope, we can see how territory is constantly being shaped and reshaped by various factors, including political ideologies, economic interests, and social norms.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to recognize the significance of territory in shaping our understanding of power. Territory is not just a physical space, but also a social and political construct that is deeply intertwined with power dynamics. By understanding the envelope and the complexities of territory, we can gain a deeper understanding of the power dynamics at play in our world.

## Chapter: Territory: Spatial Reification of Power

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the concept of territory and its role in shaping power dynamics. Territory is a fundamental concept in human society, as it is the physical space that is claimed and controlled by a group or individual. It is a crucial aspect of power, as it allows for the exercise of control and dominance over others. In this chapter, we will delve into the complexities of territory and its impact on power dynamics.

We will begin by examining the definition of territory and its various meanings. We will then explore the historical and cultural context of territory, and how it has evolved over time. We will also discuss the different types of territory, such as physical, social, and psychological territory, and how they interact with each other.

Next, we will delve into the concept of spatial reification of power. This refers to the process by which power is embodied and manifested in physical space. We will explore how territory is used as a tool for asserting and maintaining power, and how it is used to create and reinforce social hierarchies.

Finally, we will examine the role of territory in conflict and conflict resolution. We will discuss how territory is used as a source of conflict and how it can be used as a tool for resolving conflicts. We will also explore the concept of territorial integrity and its importance in international relations.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper understanding of the complexities of territory and its role in shaping power dynamics. They will also gain insight into the various factors that contribute to the creation and maintenance of territory, and how it is used to assert and maintain power. 


# Title: Territory: Spatial Reification of Power

## Chapter 20: The Map




### Section: 19.2 The Production of Territory:

### Subsection: 19.2a Techniques of Territorial Production

The production of territory is a complex process that involves various techniques and strategies. These techniques are used to create and maintain territorial boundaries, control access to resources, and establish power dynamics within a given space. In this section, we will explore some of the key techniques used in the production of territory.

#### Spatial Reification

Spatial reification is a technique used to create and maintain territorial boundaries. It involves the physical manifestation of power and control over a specific space. This can be seen in the construction of walls, fences, and other physical barriers that mark the boundaries of a territory. These barriers serve as a visual representation of power and control, reinforcing the idea of territorial ownership.

#### Legal and Political Boundaries

Legal and political boundaries are another important technique in the production of territory. These boundaries are established through laws and agreements between different political entities. They can be seen in the creation of international borders, state lines, and other legal boundaries. These boundaries are often reinforced through legal and political mechanisms, such as treaties and agreements.

#### Resource Control

Resource control is a key technique in the production of territory. It involves the management and distribution of resources within a given space. This can include the control of natural resources, such as land, water, and minerals, as well as the control of human resources, such as labor and population. By controlling access to resources, territorial powers can exert their dominance and maintain their control over a given space.

#### Military Presence

Military presence is a crucial technique in the production of territory. It involves the use of military forces to establish and maintain territorial boundaries. This can include the deployment of troops, the construction of military bases, and the use of military technology, such as surveillance and defense systems. Military presence serves as a physical manifestation of power and control, reinforcing territorial boundaries and deterring potential threats.

#### Cultural and Social Boundaries

Cultural and social boundaries are also important in the production of territory. These boundaries are established through cultural and social norms, values, and practices. They can be seen in the creation of cultural identities, language barriers, and social hierarchies. These boundaries can serve as a means of exclusion and inclusion, reinforcing territorial boundaries and establishing power dynamics within a given space.

In conclusion, the production of territory involves a complex interplay of various techniques and strategies. These techniques work together to create and maintain territorial boundaries, control access to resources, and establish power dynamics within a given space. By understanding these techniques, we can gain a deeper understanding of the role of territory in shaping power dynamics and social relations.





### Section: 19.3 Cartography and Spatial Calculation:

### Subsection: 19.3a Techniques of Cartographic Representation

Cartography is a crucial tool in the production of territory. It involves the creation of maps and other visual representations of space. These representations are used to communicate information about a territory, such as its boundaries, resources, and power dynamics. In this section, we will explore some of the key techniques used in cartographic representation.

#### Generalization

Generalization is a technique used to simplify complex spatial data for representation on a map. This is necessary because maps are two-dimensional representations of three-dimensional space, and therefore cannot accurately represent all details of a territory. Generalization involves reducing the amount of detail in the data, while still maintaining its essential features. This can be achieved through techniques such as simplification, aggregation, and abstraction.

#### Symbolization

Symbolization is a technique used to represent different features of a territory on a map. This is achieved through the use of symbols, which can represent anything from physical features such as mountains and rivers, to abstract concepts such as population density and economic activity. The choice of symbols is crucial in conveying information effectively and accurately.

#### Projection

Projection is a technique used to represent the curved surface of the Earth on a flat map. This is necessary because maps are flat surfaces, and therefore cannot accurately represent the curved surface of the Earth. Projection involves flattening the Earth's surface onto a plane, which results in distortion of the representation. The choice of projection is important in determining the accuracy and usefulness of a map.

#### Spatial Calculation

Spatial calculation is a technique used to perform mathematical operations on spatial data. This can include operations such as interpolation, extrapolation, and spatial analysis. Spatial calculation is a powerful tool in cartography, as it allows for the creation of complex and detailed maps. However, it also requires a deep understanding of mathematical principles and techniques.

In the next section, we will explore some of the key techniques used in spatial calculation, including interpolation, extrapolation, and spatial analysis. We will also discuss the challenges and limitations of these techniques, and how they can be overcome.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of the envelope and its role in spatial reification of power. We have seen how the envelope serves as a boundary, defining the extent of a territory and delineating the power dynamics within it. We have also discussed the various factors that contribute to the formation of an envelope, such as physical barriers, cultural boundaries, and political borders.

The envelope is a crucial aspect of territory, as it not only defines the physical boundaries but also represents the power dynamics within a space. It is a dynamic concept, constantly evolving and adapting to changes in the environment and society. The envelope is also a powerful tool for understanding and analyzing the complex interplay between space and power.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to note that the envelope is just one of the many aspects of territory that we have explored in this book. The concept of territory is a multifaceted one, and it is essential to understand all its dimensions to fully grasp its significance. The envelope serves as a foundation for further exploration and analysis of territory, and we hope that this chapter has provided a solid understanding of this crucial concept.

## Chapter: Territory: Spatial Reification of Power

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the concept of territory and its role in spatial reification of power. Territory is a fundamental concept in geography and political science, and it has been studied extensively by scholars from various disciplines. It refers to a specific area of land or water that is claimed and controlled by a particular group or entity. This can include countries, states, provinces, and even smaller communities such as villages or neighborhoods.

The study of territory is crucial in understanding the dynamics of power and how it is exercised in different spaces. It allows us to examine the ways in which power is spatialized and how it shapes the interactions between different groups and entities. By studying territory, we can gain insights into the complex relationships between space, power, and politics.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various aspects of territory, including its definition, characteristics, and the different types of territories that exist. We will also explore the historical and contemporary significance of territory in shaping political boundaries and power dynamics. Additionally, we will examine the role of territory in conflict and how it is used as a tool for asserting dominance and control.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of territory and its importance in the study of power and politics. By the end, readers will have a deeper appreciation for the complexities of territory and its role in shaping the world around us.

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the complex relationship between the state and the nation, two fundamental concepts in the study of territoriality. The state, as a political entity, is responsible for governing a specific territory and its inhabitants. On the other hand, the nation is a cultural and social construct that binds people together based on shared history, language, and cultural practices. The interplay between these two concepts is crucial in understanding the dynamics of territoriality and how power is spatially reified.

The state and the nation are often intertwined, with the state claiming to represent the nation and its interests. However, this relationship is not always straightforward, and conflicts can arise when the interests of the state and the nation are not aligned. This chapter will delve into these complexities, examining how the state and the nation shape each other and the implications of this relationship for territoriality.

We will also explore the concept of nationalism, a political ideology that emphasizes the importance of the nation and its interests. Nationalism can be a powerful force in shaping territoriality, as it often leads to the creation of states that align with the boundaries of the nation. However, nationalism can also lead to conflict and territorial disputes, as different nations may claim the same territory.

Finally, we will examine the role of territoriality in the formation and maintenance of the state and the nation. Territoriality is a fundamental aspect of both concepts, as it provides the physical space for the state to govern and the nation to exist. We will discuss how territoriality is used to assert power and control, and how it can be a source of conflict and competition.

In this chapter, we will use a variety of sources, including historical examples, case studies, and theoretical frameworks, to provide a comprehensive understanding of the relationship between the state and the nation. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper understanding of how these two concepts shape territoriality and the role of territoriality in shaping the state and the nation.




### Subsection: 20.1 Power & Space:

#### 20.1a Power Dynamics

Power dynamics in the context of state and nation are complex and multifaceted. They are shaped by a variety of factors, including historical, cultural, economic, and political influences. In this section, we will explore the power dynamics between the state and the nation, and how they influence territoriality.

The state, as a political entity, holds a significant amount of power. It is responsible for governing a specific territory and its inhabitants. The state's power is derived from its ability to make and enforce laws, collect taxes, and provide public services. The state also has the power to define the boundaries of its territory and to control the movement of people and goods across these boundaries.

However, the state's power is not absolute. It is subject to various constraints, including international law, public opinion, and the power of other states. For example, the state's power to define its territory is limited by international law, which recognizes the right of self-determination of peoples. This means that a state cannot unilaterally change the boundaries of its territory without the consent of the people living within those boundaries.

The nation, on the other hand, is a cultural and social construct that binds people together based on shared history, language, and cultural practices. The power of the nation is derived from its ability to mobilize its members for collective action. The nation can exert power through various means, including political lobbying, social activism, and cultural influence.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation can be complex and often involve a delicate balance of power. The state may use its power to suppress the nation, or the nation may use its power to challenge the state. However, in many cases, the state and the nation work together to achieve common goals.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation also have significant implications for territoriality. The state's power to define and control its territory can shape the boundaries of the nation. Conversely, the nation's power to mobilize its members can influence the state's policies and actions within its territory.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the power dynamics between the state and the nation, exploring how they shape territoriality and the implications of these dynamics for the study of territoriality.

#### 20.1b Power Geometries

Power geometries in the context of state and nation are spatial representations of power dynamics. They provide a visual framework for understanding the distribution and exercise of power within a territory. Power geometries are not static, but rather dynamic and fluid, reflecting the ongoing interactions and struggles for power between different actors and groups.

Power geometries can be represented in various ways, including maps, diagrams, and networks. These representations can provide valuable insights into the power dynamics within a territory, revealing patterns of power concentration and dispersion, as well as the interconnections and dependencies between different actors and groups.

For example, a power map of a state might show the distribution of power among different political parties, interest groups, and social classes. It might also show the power dynamics between the state and other actors, such as multinational corporations, non-governmental organizations, and international institutions.

Similarly, a power map of a nation might show the distribution of power among different ethnic groups, religious communities, and linguistic groups. It might also show the power dynamics between the nation and other actors, such as neighboring nations, diaspora communities, and international organizations.

Power geometries can also be used to analyze the territorial implications of power dynamics. For instance, they can reveal the spatial patterns of power concentration and dispersion, showing where power is most concentrated and where it is most dispersed. They can also reveal the spatial implications of power struggles, showing how power struggles can shape the boundaries and dynamics of territories.

However, it is important to note that power geometries are not without their limitations. They are based on simplifications and assumptions, and they can only provide a partial and partial view of power dynamics. Therefore, they should be used with caution and supplemented with other methods and perspectives.

In conclusion, power geometries provide a valuable tool for understanding the power dynamics within a territory. They can help us to visualize and analyze the complex and multifaceted power dynamics between the state and the nation, and their territorial implications.

#### 20.1c Power & Territory

Power and territory are intrinsically linked, with power often being used to define and control territory. The state, as a political entity, holds the power to define its territory and control the movement of people and goods across its boundaries. This power is often exercised through various means, including legal frameworks, physical barriers, and surveillance technologies.

The state's power over territory is not absolute, however. It is subject to various constraints, including international law, public opinion, and the power of other states. For example, the state's power to define its territory is limited by international law, which recognizes the right of self-determination of peoples. This means that a state cannot unilaterally change the boundaries of its territory without the consent of the people living within those boundaries.

The nation, as a cultural and social construct, also plays a significant role in shaping the power dynamics of territory. The nation can exert power through various means, including political lobbying, social activism, and cultural influence. For instance, a nation might use its cultural influence to challenge the state's definition of territory, asserting its own territorial claims based on historical, cultural, or emotional connections.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation can be complex and often involve a delicate balance of power. The state may use its power to suppress the nation, or the nation may use its power to challenge the state. However, in many cases, the state and the nation work together to achieve common goals, such as defending the nation's territory or promoting the nation's interests.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation also have significant implications for territoriality. The state's power to define and control territory can shape the boundaries and dynamics of the nation, influencing the nation's sense of identity, belonging, and territoriality. Conversely, the nation's power to assert its territorial claims can influence the state's policies and actions, shaping the state's territorial practices and policies.

In conclusion, power and territory are deeply intertwined, with power often being used to define and control territory. The power dynamics between the state and the nation play a crucial role in shaping the boundaries and dynamics of territory, influencing the territorial practices and policies of both the state and the nation.

#### 20.2a State Power

The state, as a political entity, holds a significant amount of power. This power is often used to define and control territory, as well as to shape the boundaries and dynamics of the nation. The state's power is derived from its ability to make and enforce laws, collect taxes, and provide public services. It is also derived from its ability to define and control its territory, as well as to influence the territorial dynamics of the nation.

The state's power over territory is not absolute, however. It is subject to various constraints, including international law, public opinion, and the power of other states. For example, the state's power to define its territory is limited by international law, which recognizes the right of self-determination of peoples. This means that a state cannot unilaterally change the boundaries of its territory without the consent of the people living within those boundaries.

The state's power over territory is also influenced by the power of the nation. The nation, as a cultural and social construct, can exert power through various means, including political lobbying, social activism, and cultural influence. For instance, a nation might use its cultural influence to challenge the state's definition of territory, asserting its own territorial claims based on historical, cultural, or emotional connections.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation can be complex and often involve a delicate balance of power. The state may use its power to suppress the nation, or the nation may use its power to challenge the state. However, in many cases, the state and the nation work together to achieve common goals, such as defending the nation's territory or promoting the nation's interests.

The power dynamics between the state and the nation also have significant implications for territoriality. The state's power to define and control territory can shape the boundaries and dynamics of the nation, influencing the nation's sense of identity, belonging, and territoriality. Conversely, the nation's power to assert its territorial claims can influence the state's policies and actions, shaping the state's territorial practices and policies.

In conclusion, state power plays a crucial role in shaping territoriality. It is a complex and dynamic concept, influenced by a variety of factors, including international law, public opinion, and the power of the nation. Understanding state power is therefore essential for understanding territoriality and the power dynamics between the state and the nation.

#### 20.3a Nation Power

The nation, as a cultural and social construct, also holds a significant amount of power. The power dynamics between the state and the nation can be complex and often involve a delicate balance of power. Conversely, the state's power to define and control territory can shape the boundaries and dynamics of the nation, influencing the nation's sense of identity, belonging, and territoriality.

In conclusion, both the state and the nation hold significant power, and their power dynamics have a profound impact on territoriality. Understanding these power dynamics is crucial for understanding territoriality and the complex interplay between state and nation.

The tension between these two concepts is a fundamental aspect of territoriality, as it influences the ways in which space is perceived, experienced, and controlled.

We have also examined how territoriality is not a static concept, but rather a dynamic and fluid process. It is shaped by a multitude of factors, including historical events, political ideologies, cultural practices, and economic forces. The state and the nation are not the only actors in this process, but they are two of the most influential ones. Their power struggles and collaborations shape the territorial landscape in profound ways.

In conclusion, territoriality is a complex and multifaceted concept that is deeply intertwined with the state and the nation. Understanding the dynamics of state and nation is therefore crucial for understanding territoriality. It is a process that is constantly evolving, shaped by a multitude of factors, and influenced by the power struggles and collaborations of the state and the nation.
